if(google_ads.length
!=
0)
{








apply_ad_config(google_ads.length);









render_ads(true,
window['ad_config_top']);









if(window['backfillParam'])
{












window['backfillParam']['pl_rnum']
=
google_ads.length;












window['backfillParam']['pl_time']
=
Date.now()
-
afc_ad_start_time;








}




}
}

function
apply_ad_config(num)
{
window['ad_config_top']
=
Math.min(2,
num);
window['ad_config_bot']
=
Math.min(2,
num);
}

google_ad_client
=
'ca-aj-cat';
google_ad_channel
=
'cx_ask_wiki,ad_dirN';
google_ad_output
=
'js';
google_max_num_ads
=
'4';
google_ad_type
=
'text';
google_image_size
=
'';
google_num_ads_recieved=
'';
google_language
=
'';
google_country
=
'';
google_encoding
=
'utf8';
google_safe
=
'medium';
google_adtest
=
'off';
google_ad_section
=
'default';
google_page_url
=
'';
google_hints
=
'Green_Day';
google_kw
=
'';
google_kw_type
=
'broad';


var
backfillParam
=
{




pl_rqnum
:
google_max_num_ads,




pl_hints
:
google_hints,




pl_rp
:
"false",




pl_kw
:
google_kw,




pl_cl
:
google_ad_client,




pl_ch
:
google_ad_channel,




pl_hex
:
"#FDFEEE",




pl_type
:
"afc",




pl_clksp
:
"none"};

var
word_arr
;

var
word_arr_len
;


function
highlightQuery(input_str)
{

var
queryTokenArray
=
"green,_,day,";


var
tok_arr
=
queryTokenArray.split(",");

for(tok_arr_idx=0;
tok_arr_idx
<
tok_arr.length-1;
tok_arr_idx
++)
{

if(isCombinationWord(tok_arr[tok_arr_idx])){
word_arr
=
tok_arr[tok_arr_idx].split("-");
word_arr_len
=
word_arr.length;
first_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(word_arr[0],0);

if(first_pos
!=-1)
{
input_str
=
highlightCombinationWords(input_str,first_pos);
}
}
else
{
first_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(tok_arr[tok_arr_idx],0);
if(first_pos
!=
-1
&&
tok_arr[tok_arr_idx].length
>
0)
{
input_str
=
highlightSimpleWords(input_str,tok_arr[tok_arr_idx],first_pos);
}
}
}
return
input_str;
}

function
isCombinationWord(word){
if(word.indexOf("-")
!=
-1){
return
true;
}
else
{
return
false;
}
}


function
isAlpha(ch)
{
if
(ch
!=
null
&&
ch.match(/^[a-zA-Z0-9]+$/)){
return
true;
}
return
false;
}

function
isQueryinInput(firstindex,
input_str,
j){
for(i=firstindex;
i<
input_str.length
;
++i)
{
var
currindex
=
i;

if(!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(i)))
{
if(firstindex
==
currindex)

{
firstindex++;
}
else
{
if(word_arr[j]
!=
input_str.substring(firstindex,currindex).toLowerCase())
return
-1;
if
(j
==
word_arr_len-1)
return
currindex;
else
return
isQueryinInput(currindex+1,input_str,++j);
}
}
}

if(j
<
word_arr_len)
{
if(word_arr[j]
!=
input_str.substring(firstindex,currindex+1).toLowerCase())
return
-1;
}

return
(currindex
+
1)
;
}


function

highlightCombinationWords(input_str,first_pos)
{
exactmatch
=
isQueryinInput(first_pos+word_arr[0].length,input_str,1)
;
if(exactmatch
!=-1
)

{
bold_str
=
"<b>"
+
input_str.substring(first_pos,exactmatch)
+
"</b>";
input_str
=
input_str.substring(0,first_pos)
+
bold_str
+
input_str.substring(exactmatch);
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(word_arr[0],exactmatch+7);
while(next_pos
!=
-1)
{
return
highlightCombinationWords(input_str,next_pos);
}
}
return
input_str;
}


function

highlightSimpleWords(input_str,token,
first_pos)
{
var
end_pos
=
first_pos
+
token.length;
if(!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(end_pos))
&&
!isAlpha(input_str.charAt(first_pos-1))){
bold_str
=
"<b>"
+
input_str.substring(first_pos,end_pos)
+
"</b>";
input_str
=
input_str.substring(0,first_pos)
+
bold_str
+
input_str.substring(end_pos);
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(token,end_pos+7);
}
else
{
next_pos
=
input_str.toLowerCase().indexOf(token,end_pos);
}

while(next_pos
!=
-1)
{
return
highlightSimpleWords(input_str,token,next_pos);
}
return
input_str;
}</script>

<p><b>Green
Day</b>
is
an
American
<a
href="/wiki/Punk_rock?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Punk
rock">punk
rock</a>
band
formed
in
1987.
The
band
consists
of
lead
vocalist
and
guitarist
<a
href="/wiki/Billie_Joe_Armstrong?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billie
Joe
Armstrong">Billie
Joe
Armstrong</a>,
bassist
and
backing
vocalist
<a
href="/wiki/Mike_Dirnt?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mike
Dirnt">Mike
Dirnt</a>,
drummer
<a
href="/wiki/Tr%C3%A9_Cool?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tr&eacute;
Cool">Tr&eacute;
Cool</a>
and
guitarist
and
backing
vocalist
<a
href="/wiki/Jason_White_(musician)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jason
White
(musician)">Jason
White</a>,
who
became
a
full
member
after
playing
in
the
band
as
a
session
and
touring
guitarist
for
13
years.<sup
id="cite_ref-Alan_Di_Perna_1-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Alan_Di_Perna-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup>
Cool
replaced
former
drummer
<a
href="/wiki/John_Kiffmeyer?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="John
Kiffmeyer">John
Kiffmeyer</a>
in
1990,
prior
to
the
recording
of
the
band's
second
studio
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Kerplunk_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Kerplunk
(album)">Kerplunk</a></i>
(1992).</p>








<p>Green
Day
was
originally
part
of
the
punk
scene
at
the
DIY
<a
href="/wiki/924_Gilman_Street?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="924
Gilman
Street">924
Gilman
Street</a>
club
in
<a
href="/wiki/Berkeley,_California?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Berkeley,
California">Berkeley,
California</a>.
The
band's
early
releases
were
from
the
<a
href="/wiki/Independent_record_label?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Independent
record
label">independent
record
label</a>
<a
href="/wiki/Lookout!_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lookout!
Records">Lookout!
Records</a>.
In
1994,
its
major
label
debut
<i><a
href="/wiki/Dookie?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dookie">Dookie</a></i>
released
through
<a
href="/wiki/Reprise_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Reprise
Records">Reprise
Records</a>
became
a
breakout
success
and
eventually
sold
over
10
million
copies
in
the
U.S.<sup
id="cite_ref-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup>
Green
Day
was
widely
credited,
alongside
fellow
<a
href="/wiki/Punk_rock_in_California?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Punk
rock
in
California">California
punk</a>
bands
<a
href="/wiki/Sublime_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sublime
(band)">Sublime</a>,<sup
id="cite_ref-3"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup>
<a
href="/wiki/Bad_Religion?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bad
Religion">Bad
Religion</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/The_Offspring?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Offspring">The
Offspring</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Rancid_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rancid
(band)">Rancid</a>,
with
popularizing
and
reviving
mainstream
interest
in
punk
rock
in
the
United
States.<sup
id="cite_ref-4"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-punk_revival_5-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-punk_revival-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Green
Day's
three
follow-up
albums,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Insomniac_(Green_Day_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Insomniac
(Green
Day
album)">Insomniac</a></i>
(1995),
<i><a
href="/wiki/Nimrod_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nimrod
(album)">Nimrod</a></i>
(1997),
and
<i><a
href="/wiki/Warning_(Green_Day_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Warning
(Green
Day
album)">Warning</a></i>
(2000)
did
not
achieve
the
massive
success
of
<i>Dookie,</i>
though
they
were
still
successful,
with
<i>Insomniac</i>
and
<i>Nimrod</i>
reaching
double
platinum
and
<i>Warning</i>
reaching
gold
status.<sup
id="cite_ref-Timeline_6-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Timeline-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band's
<a
href="/wiki/Rock_opera?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rock
opera">rock
opera</a>,
<i><a
href="/wiki/American_Idiot?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="American
Idiot">American
Idiot</a></i>
(2004),
reignited
the
band's
popularity
with
a
younger
generation,
selling
five
million
copies
in
the
United
States.<sup
id="cite_ref-Timeline_6-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Timeline-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band's
eighth
studio
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/21st_Century_Breakdown?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="21st
Century
Breakdown">21st
Century
Breakdown</a></i>,
was
released
in
2009
which
achieved
the
band's
best
chart
performance
to
date.<sup
id="cite_ref-7"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup>
<i>21st
Century
Breakdown</i>
was
followed
up
by
a
trilogy
of
albums
called
<i><a
href="/wiki/%C2%A1Uno!?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="&iexcl;Uno!">&iexcl;Uno!</a></i>,
<i><a
href="/wiki/%C2%A1Dos!?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="&iexcl;Dos!">&iexcl;Dos!</a></i>,
and
<i><a
href="/wiki/%C2%A1Tr%C3%A9!?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="&iexcl;Tr&eacute;!">&iexcl;Tr&eacute;!</a></i>
released
in
September,
November
and
December
2012
respectively.<sup
id="cite_ref-Album_Trio_Press_Release_8-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Album_Trio_Press_Release-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>They
are
one
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_music_artists?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="List
of
best-selling
music
artists">world's
best-selling
groups
of
all
time</a>,
having
sold
over
75
million
albums
worldwide.<sup
id="cite_ref-9"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
group
has
won
five
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Awards"
class="mw-redirect">Grammy
Awards</a>:
<a
href="/wiki/Best_Alternative_Music_Album?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Best
Alternative
Music
Album"
class="mw-redirect">Best
Alternative
Album</a>
for
<i><a
href="/wiki/Dookie?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dookie">Dookie</a></i>,
<a
href="/wiki/Best_Rock_Album?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Best
Rock
Album"
class="mw-redirect">Best
Rock
Album</a>
for
<i><a
href="/wiki/American_Idiot?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="American
Idiot">American
Idiot</a></i>,
<a
href="/wiki/Record_of_the_Year?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Record
of
the
Year"
class="mw-redirect">Record
of
the
Year</a>
for
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Boulevard_of_Broken_Dreams_(Green_Day_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Boulevard
of
Broken
Dreams
(Green
Day
song)">Boulevard
of
Broken
Dreams</a>&quot;,
Best
Rock
Album
for
the
second
time
for
<i><a
href="/wiki/21st_Century_Breakdown?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="21st
Century
Breakdown">21st
Century
Breakdown</a></i>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Best_Musical_Show_Album?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Best
Musical
Show
Album"
class="mw-redirect">Best
Musical
Show
Album</a>
for
<i><a
href="/wiki/American_Idiot:_The_Original_Broadway_Cast_Recording?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="American
Idiot:
The
Original
Broadway
Cast
Recording">American
Idiot:
The
Original
Broadway
Cast
Recording</a></i>.
In
2010,
a
<a
href="/wiki/American_Idiot_(musical)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="American
Idiot
(musical)">stage
adaptation</a>
of
<i>American
Idiot</i>
debuted
on
Broadway.
The
musical
was
nominated
for
three
<a
href="/wiki/Tony_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tony
Awards"
class="mw-redirect">Tony
Awards</a>:
<a
href="/wiki/Tony_Award_for_Best_Musical?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tony
Award
for
Best
Musical">Best
Musical</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Tony_Award_for_Best_Scenic_Design?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tony
Award
for
Best
Scenic
Design">Best
Scenic
Design</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Tony_Award_for_Best_Lighting_Design?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tony
Award
for
Best
Lighting
Design">Best
Lighting
Design</a>,
losing
only
the
first.
Also
in
2010,
Green
Day
were
ranked
number
91
in
the
<i><a
href="/wiki/VH1?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="VH1">VH1</a></i>
list
of
the
&quot;100
Greatest
Artists
of
All
Time&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-10"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="History">History</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Green_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1"
title="Edit
section:
History">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Formation_and_Lookout.21_years_.281987.E2.80.931993.29">Formation
and
Lookout!
years
(1987â€“1993)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Green_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2"
title="Edit
section:
Formation
and
Lookout!
years
(1987â€“1993)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>In
1987,
friends
Billie
Joe
Armstrong
and
Mike
Dirnt,
15
years
old
at
the
time,
formed
a
band
called
Sweet
Children.<sup
id="cite_ref-11"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup>
Its
first
live
performance
took
place
on
October
17,
1987
at
Rod's
Hickory
Pit
in
<a
href="/wiki/Vallejo,_California?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Vallejo,
California">Vallejo,
California</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-Vhawk_12-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Vhawk-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
1988,
Armstrong
and
Dirnt
began
working
with
Sean
Hughes
and
the
former
<a
href="/wiki/Isocracy_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Isocracy
(band)">Isocracy</a>
drummer
<a
href="/wiki/John_Kiffmeyer?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="John
Kiffmeyer">John
Kiffmeyer</a>,
also
known
as
&quot;Al
Sobrante&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-Kimpel2006_13-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Kimpel2006-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup>
As
said
in
the
film
<i><a
href="/wiki/Punk%27s_Not_Dead_(2007_film)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Punk's
Not
Dead
(2007
film)">Punk's
Not
Dead</a></i>,
Armstrong
cites
the
band
<a
href="/wiki/Operation_Ivy_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Operation
Ivy
(band)">Operation
Ivy</a>
(which
featured
<a
href="/wiki/Tim_Armstrong?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tim
Armstrong">Tim
Armstrong</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Matt_Freeman?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Matt
Freeman">Matt
Freeman</a>
of
<a
href="/wiki/Rancid_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rancid
(band)">Rancid</a>)
as
a
major
influence,
and
a
group
that
inspired
him
to
form
a
band.</p>








<p>In
1988,
<a
href="/wiki/Larry_Livermore?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Larry
Livermore">Larry
Livermore</a>,
owner
of
<a
href="/wiki/Lookout!_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lookout!
Records">Lookout!
Records</a>,
saw
the
band
play
an
early
show
and
signed
the
group
to
his
label.
In
1989,
the
band
recorded
its
debut
<a
href="/wiki/Extended_play?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Extended
play">extended
play</a>,
<i><a
href="/wiki/1,000_Hours?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="1,000
Hours">1,000
Hours</a></i>.
Before
<i>1,000
Hours</i>
was
released,
the
group
dropped
the
name
Sweet
Children;
according
to
Livermore,
this
was
done
to
avoid
confusion
with
another
local
band
<a
href="/wiki/Sweet_Baby?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sweet
Baby">Sweet
Baby</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-14"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band
adopted
the
name
Green
Day,
due
to
their
fondness
for
<a
href="/wiki/Marijuana?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Marijuana"
class="mw-redirect">marijuana</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-15"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Lookout!
would
release
Green
Day's
debut
studio
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/39/Smooth?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="39/Smooth">39/Smooth</a></i>
in
early
1990.
Green
Day
would
record
two
extended
plays
later
that
year,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Slappy?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Slappy">Slappy</a></i>
and
<i><a
href="/wiki/Sweet_Children_(EP)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sweet
Children
(EP)">Sweet
Children</a></i>,
the
latter
of
which
included
older
songs
that
the
band
had
recorded
for
the
<a
href="/wiki/Minneapolis?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Minneapolis">Minneapolis</a>
independent
record
label
Skene!
Records.
In
1991,
Lookout!
Records
re-released
<i>39/Smooth</i>
under
the
name
<i>1,039/Smoothed
Out
Slappy
Hours,</i>
and
added
the
songs
from
the
band's
first
two
EPs,
<i>Slappy</i>,
and
<i>1,000
Hours</i>.
In
late
1990,
shortly
after
the
band's
first
nationwide
tour,
Sobrante
left
the
East
Bay
area
to
attend
college.<sup
id="cite_ref-Vhawk_12-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Vhawk-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup>
<a
href="/wiki/The_Lookouts?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Lookouts">The
Lookouts</a>
drummer
<a
href="/wiki/Tr%C3%A9_Cool?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tr&eacute;
Cool">Tr&eacute;
Cool</a>
began
filling
in
as
a
temporary
replacement
and
later
Cool's
position
as
Green
Day's
drummer
became
permanent.<sup
id="cite_ref-Vhawk_12-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Vhawk-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band
went
on
tour
for
most
of
1992
and
1993,
and
played
a
number
of
shows
overseas
in
Europe.
The
band's
second
studio
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Kerplunk_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Kerplunk
(album)">Kerplunk</a></i>
sold
50,000
copies
in
the
U.S.<sup
id="cite_ref-16"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Breakthrough_success_.281994.E2.80.931996.29">Breakthrough
success
(1994â€“1996)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Green_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3"
title="Edit
section:
Breakthrough
success
(1994â€“1996)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<div
class="thumb
tleft">









<div
class="thumbinner"
style="width:172px;">









<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Normal_180914_1994-XX-XX_-_Green_Day_Live_.jpg"
target="_blank"
class="image"><img
alt=""
src="http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Normal_180914_1994-XX-XX_-_Green_Day_Live_.jpg/170px-Normal_180914_1994-XX-XX_-_Green_Day_Live_.jpg"
width="170"
height="209"
class="thumbimage"
srcset="http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Normal_180914_1994-XX-XX_-_Green_Day_Live_.jpg/255px-Normal_180914_1994-XX-XX_-_Green_Day_Live_.jpg
1.5x,
http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/6/6b/Normal_180914_1994-XX-XX_-_Green_Day_Live_.jpg
2x"
/></a>










<div
class="thumbcaption">











<div
class="magnify">











<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Normal_180914_1994-XX-XX_-_Green_Day_Live_.jpg"
target="_blank"
class="internal"
title="Enlarge"><img
src="http://sp.ask.com/sh/i/wiki/magnify-clip.png"
width="15"
height="11"
alt=""
/></a>










</div>
Armstrong
performing
in
1994.









</div>









</div>








</div>








<p><i>Kerplunk'</i>s
underground
success
led
to
a
number
of
major
record
labels
being
interested
in
signing
Green
Day,
and
the
band
eventually
left
Lookout!
and
signed
to
<a
href="/wiki/Reprise_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Reprise
Records">Reprise
Records</a>
after
attracting
the
attention
of
producer
<a
href="/wiki/Rob_Cavallo?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rob
Cavallo">Rob
Cavallo</a>.
The
group
was
impressed
by
his
work
with
fellow
Californian
band
<a
href="/wiki/The_Muffs?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Muffs">The
Muffs</a>,
and
later
remarked
that
Cavallo
&quot;was
the
only
person
we
could
really
talk
to
and
connect
with&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-vh1_behind_the_music_17-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-vh1_behind_the_music-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup>
Reflecting
on
the
period,
Armstrong
told
<i><a
href="/wiki/Spin_(magazine)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Spin
(magazine)">Spin</a></i>
magazine
in
1999,
&quot;I
couldn't
go
back
to
the
punk
scene,
whether
we
were
the
biggest
success
in
the
world
or
the
biggest
failure
...
The
only
thing
I
could
do
was
get
on
my
bike
and
go
forward.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-18"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup>
After
signing
with
Reprise,
the
band
went
to
work
on
recording
its
major
label
debut,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Dookie?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dookie">Dookie</a>.</i></p>

class="mbox-small"
style="border:1px
solid
#aaa;
background-color:#f9f9f9;">

<tr>











<td
class="mbox-image">












<div
class="center">













<div

<img

1.5x,
http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg/100px-Gnome-mime-sound-openclipart.svg.png
2x"
/>












</div>












</div>
</td>











<td
class="mbox-text
plainlist"
style="line-height:1.1em;">












<div
class="haudio">













<div
style="padding:2px
0;"

<a

colspan="2"
class="mbox-text"
style="line-height:1.1em;"><span
style="font-size:smaller;"><i>Problems
playing
these

<a

help</a>.</i></span></td>

<p>Recorded
in
three
weeks,
and
released
in
February
1994,<sup
id="cite_ref-19"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup>
<i>Dookie</i>
became
a
commercial
success,
helped
by
extensive
MTV
airplay
for
the
videos
of
the
songs
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Longview_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Longview
(song)">Longview</a>&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Basket_Case_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Basket
Case
(song)">Basket
Case</a>&quot;,
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/When_I_Come_Around?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="When
I
Come
Around">When
I
Come
Around</a>&quot;,
all
of
which
reached
the
number
one
position
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/Modern_Rock_Tracks?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Modern
Rock
Tracks"
class="mw-redirect">Modern
Rock
Tracks</a>
charts.
At
a
September
9,
1994
performance
at
<a
href="/wiki/Hatch_Memorial_Shell?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hatch
Memorial
Shell">Hatch
Memorial
Shell</a>
in
Boston,
mayhem
broke-out
during
the
band's
set
(cut
short
to
seven
songs)
and
by
the
end
of
the
rampage,
100
people
were
injured
and
45
arrested.<sup
id="cite_ref-20"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band
also
joined
the
lineups
of
both
the
<a
href="/wiki/Lollapalooza?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Lollapalooza">Lollapalooza</a>
festival
and
<a
href="/wiki/Woodstock_%2794?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Woodstock
'94">Woodstock
'94</a>,
where
they
started
an
infamous
mud
fight.
During
the
concert,
a
security
guard
mistook
bassist
<a
href="/wiki/Mike_Dirnt?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mike
Dirnt">Mike
Dirnt</a>
for
a
stage-invading
fan
and
punched
out
some
of
his
teeth.<sup
id="cite_ref-21"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup>
Viewed
by
millions
by
<a
href="/wiki/Pay-per-view?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pay-per-view">pay-per-view</a>
television,
the
Woodstock
1994
performance
further
aided
Green
Day's
growing
publicity
and
recognition,<sup
id="cite_ref-vh1_behind_the_music_17-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-vh1_behind_the_music-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
helped
push
its
album
to
eventual
<a
href="/wiki/RIAA_certification?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="RIAA
certification">diamond
status</a>.
In
1995,
<i>Dookie</i>
won
the
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Award">Grammy
Award</a>
for
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Alternative_Music_Album?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Award
for
Best
Alternative
Music
Album">Best
Alternative
Album</a>
and
the
band
was
nominated
for
nine
MTV
Video
Music
Awards
including
Video
of
the
Year.</p>








<p>In
1995,
a
new
single
for
the
<i><a
href="/wiki/Angus_(film)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Angus
(film)">Angus</a></i>
soundtrack
was
released,
entitled
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/J.A.R.?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="J.A.R.">J.A.R.</a>&quot;.
The
single
debuted
at
number
one
on
the
<i>Billboard</i>
<a
href="/wiki/Modern_Rock_Tracks?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Modern
Rock
Tracks"
class="mw-redirect">Modern
Rock
Tracks</a>
chart.
The
song
was
followed
by
the
band's
fourth
studio
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Insomniac_(Green_Day_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Insomniac
(Green
Day
album)">Insomniac</a></i>,
which
was
released
in
the
fall
of
1995.
<i>Insomniac</i>
was
a
much
darker
and
heavier
response
to
the
band's
newfound
popularity,
compared
to
the
more
melodic
<i>Dookie</i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-vh1_behind_the_music_17-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-vh1_behind_the_music-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
album
opened
to
a
warm
critical
reception,
earning
4
out
of
5
stars
from
<i><a
href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rolling
Stone">Rolling
Stone</a></i>,
which
said
&quot;In
punk,
the
good
stuff
actually
unfolds
and
gains
meaning
as
you
listen
without
sacrificing
any
of
its
electric,
haywire
immediacy.
And
Green
Day
are
as
good
as
this
stuff
gets.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-22"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
singles
released
from
<i>Insomniac</i>
were
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Geek_Stink_Breath?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Geek
Stink
Breath">Geek
Stink
Breath</a>&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Stuck_with_Me?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Stuck
with
Me">Stuck
with
Me</a>&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Brain_Stew/Jaded?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Brain
Stew/Jaded"
class="mw-redirect">Brain
Stew/Jaded</a>&quot;,
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Walking_Contradiction?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Walking
Contradiction">Walking
Contradiction</a>&quot;.</p>








<p>Though
the
album
did
not
approach
the
success
of
<i>Dookie,</i>
it
sold
two
million
copies
in
the
United
States.<sup
id="cite_ref-Album_Guide_23-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Album_Guide-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
addition,
the
album
won
the
band
award
nominations
for
Favorite
Artist,
Favorite
Hard
Rock
Artist,
and
Favorite
Alternative
Artist
at
the
1996
<a
href="/wiki/American_Music_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="American
Music
Awards"
class="mw-redirect">American
Music
Awards</a>,
and
the
video
for
&quot;Walking
Contradiction&quot;
got
the
band
a
Grammy
nomination
for
Best
Video,
Short
Form,
in
addition
to
a
Best
Special
Effects
nomination
at
the
MTV
Video
Music
Awards.
After
that,
the
band
abruptly
cancelled
a
European
tour,
citing
exhaustion.<sup
id="cite_ref-snotty_24-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-snotty-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h3><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Middle_years_and_decline_in_commercial_success_.281997.E2.80.932002.29">Middle
years
and
decline
in
commercial
success
(1997â€“2002)</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Green_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4"
title="Edit
section:
Middle
years
and
decline
in
commercial
success
(1997â€“2002)">edit</a>]</span></h3>








<p>After
a
brief
hiatus
in
1996,
Green
Day
began
to
work
on
a
new
album
in
1997.
From
the
outset,
both
the
band
and
Cavallo
agreed
that
the
album
had
to
be
different
from
its
previous
albums.<sup
id="cite_ref-25"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
result
was
<i><a
href="/wiki/Nimrod_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nimrod
(album)">Nimrod</a></i>,
an
experimental
deviation
from
the
band's
standard
pop-punk
brand
of
music.
The
new
album
was
released
in
October
1997.
It
provided
a
variety
of
music,
from
pop-punk,
<a
href="/wiki/Surf_rock?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Surf
rock"
class="mw-redirect">surf
rock</a>,
and
<a
href="/wiki/Ska?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ska">ska</a>,
to
an
acoustic
ballad.
<i>Nimrod</i>
entered
the
charts
at
number
10.
The
success
of
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Good_Riddance_(Time_of_Your_Life)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Good
Riddance
(Time
of
Your
Life)">Good
Riddance
(Time
of
Your
Life)</a>&quot;
won
the
band
an
MTV
Video
Award
for
Best
Alternative
Video.
The
song
was
also
used
in
the
second
&quot;clip
show&quot;
episode
of
<i><a
href="/wiki/Seinfeld?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Seinfeld">Seinfeld</a></i>
and
on
two
episodes
of
<i><a
href="/wiki/ER_(TV_series)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="ER
(TV
series)">ER</a></i>.</p>








<p>The
other
singles
released
from
<i>Nimrod</i>
were
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Nice_Guys_Finish_Last?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Nice
Guys
Finish
Last">Nice
Guys
Finish
Last</a>&quot;,
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Hitchin%27_a_Ride_(Green_Day_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hitchin'
a
Ride
(Green
Day
song)">Hitchin'
a
Ride</a>&quot;
and
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Redundant_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Redundant
(song)">Redundant</a>&quot;.
The
band
made
a
guest
appearance
in
an
episode
of
<i><a
href="/wiki/King_of_the_Hill?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="King
of
the
Hill">King
of
the
Hill</a></i>
entitled
&quot;The
Man
Who
Shot
Cane
Skretteberg&quot;,
which
aired
in
1997.
In
late
1997
and
most
of
1998,
Green
Day
embarked
on
a
tour
in
support
of
<i>Nimrod</i>.
In
1999,
the
guitarist
<a
href="/wiki/Jason_White_(musician)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jason
White
(musician)">Jason
White</a>
began
supporting
the
band
on
the
concerts
as
rhythm
guitarist.</p>








<p>In
2000,
Green
Day
released
its
sixth
studio
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Warning_(Green_Day_album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Warning
(Green
Day
album)">Warning</a></i>.
In
support
of
the
album,
the
band
participated
in
the
<a
href="/wiki/Warped_Tour?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Warped
Tour">Warped
Tour</a>
in
2000.
The
band
also
had
an
independent
tour
to
support
the
album
in
2001.
Critics'
reviews
of
the
album
were
varied.<sup
id="cite_ref-metacritic_26-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-metacritic-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup>
<a
href="/wiki/Allmusic?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Allmusic"
class="mw-redirect">Allmusic</a>
gave
it
4.5/5
saying
&quot;<i>Warning</i>
may
not
be
an
innovative
record
per
se,
but
it's
tremendously
satisfying.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-27"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup>
<i><a
href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rolling
Stone">Rolling
Stone</a></i>
was
more
critical,
giving
it
3/5,
and
saying
&quot;<i>Warning</i>...
invites
the
question:
Who
wants
to
listen
to
songs
of
faith,
hope
and
social
commentary
from
what
used
to
be
snot-core's
biggest-selling
band?&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-28"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup>
Though
it
produced
the
hit
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Minority_(Green_Day_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Minority
(Green
Day
song)">Minority</a>&quot;
and
a
smaller
hit
with
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Warning_(Green_Day_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Warning
(Green
Day
song)">Warning</a>&quot;,
some
observers
were
coming
to
the
conclusion
that
the
band
was
losing
relevance,<sup
id="cite_ref-metacritic_26-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-metacritic-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup>
and
a
decline
in
popularity
followed.
While
all
of
Green
Day's
previous
albums
had
reached
a
status
of
at
least
double
platinum,
<i>Warning</i>
was
only
certified
platinum.</p>








<p>At
the
2001
California
Music
Awards,
Green
Day
won
all
eight
of
the
awards
that
it
was
nominated
for.<sup
id="cite_ref-cal2001_29-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-cal2001-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
group
won
the
awards
for
Outstanding
Album
(<i>Warning</i>),
Outstanding
Punk
Rock/Ska
Album
(<i>Warning</i>),
Outstanding
Group,
Outstanding
Male
Vocalist,
Outstanding
Bassist,
Outstanding
Drummer,
Outstanding
Songwriter,
and
Outstanding
Artist.<sup
id="cite_ref-30"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>The
release
of
two
compilation
albums,
<i><a
href="/wiki/International_Superhits!?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="International
Superhits!">International
Superhits!</a></i>
and
<i><a
href="/wiki/Shenanigans_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Shenanigans
(album)">Shenanigans</a></i>,
followed
<i>Warning</i>.
<i>International
Superhits</i>
and
its
companion
collection
of
music
videos,
<i><a
href="/wiki/International_Supervideos!?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="International
Supervideos!"
class="mw-redirect">International
Supervideos!</a></i>.
<i>Shenanigans</i>
contained
some
of
the
band's
b-sides,
including
&quot;Espionage&quot;,
which
was
featured
in
the
film
<i><a
href="/wiki/Austin_Powers:_The_Spy_Who_Shagged_Me?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Austin
Powers:
The
Spy
Who
Shagged
Me">Austin
Powers:
The
Spy
Who
Shagged
Me</a></i>
and
was
nominated
for
a
<a
href="/wiki/Grammy_Award_for_Best_Rock_Instrumental_Performance?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Grammy
Award
for
Best
Rock
Instrumental
Performance">Grammy
Award
for
Best
Rock
Instrumental
Performance</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-cal2001_29-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-cal2001-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
the
spring
of
2002,
Green
Day
co-headlined
the
<a
href="/wiki/Pop_Disaster_Tour?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pop
Disaster
Tour">Pop
Disaster
Tour</a>
with
<a
href="/wiki/Blink-182?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Blink-182">Blink-182</a>
which
was
documented
on
the
DVD
<i>Riding
in
Vans
with
Boys</i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-31"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<p>In
the
summer
of
2003,
the
band
went
into
a
studio
to
write
and
record
new
material
for
a
new
album,
tentatively
titled
<i><a
href="/wiki/Cigarettes_and_Valentines?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cigarettes
and
Valentines">Cigarettes
and
Valentines</a>.</i><sup
id="cite_ref-32"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup>
After
completing
20
tracks,
the
<a
href="/wiki/Master_recording?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Master
recording"
class="mw-redirect">master
recordings</a>
were
stolen
from
the
studio.
Instead
of
re-recording
the
stolen
tracks,
the
band
decided
to
abandon
the
entire
project
and
start
over,
considering
the
material
to
be
unrepresentative
of
the
band's
best
work.<sup
id="cite_ref-Cigarettes_33-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Cigarettes-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup>
It
was
then
revealed
that
a
band
called
<a
href="/wiki/The_Network?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Network">The
Network</a>
was
signed
to
Armstrong's
record
label
<a
href="/wiki/Adeline_Records?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Adeline
Records">Adeline
Records</a>
with
little
fanfare
and
information.
After
the
mysterious
band
released
an
album
called
<i><a
href="/wiki/Money_Money_2020?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Money
Money
2020">Money
Money
2020</a></i>,
it
was
rumored
that
The
Network
was
a
Green
Day
side
project,
due
to
the
similarities
in
the
bands'
sounds.<sup
id="cite_ref-MTVNews_34-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-MTVNews-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup>
However,
these
rumors
were
never
addressed
by
the
band
or
Adeline
Records,
except
for
a
statement
on
the
Adeline
website
discussing
an
ongoing
dispute
between
the
two
bands.<sup
id="cite_ref-MTVNews_34-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-MTVNews-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Green
Day
collaborated
with
<a
href="/wiki/Iggy_Pop?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Iggy
Pop">Iggy
Pop</a>
on
two
tracks
for
his
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Skull_Ring?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Skull
Ring">Skull
Ring</a></i>
in
November
2003.
On
February
1,
2004
a
new
song,
a
cover
of
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/I_Fought_the_Law?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="I
Fought
the
Law">I
Fought
the
Law</a>&quot;
made
its
debut
on
a
commercial
for
<a
href="/wiki/ITunes?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="ITunes">iTunes</a>
during
<a
href="/wiki/NFL?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="NFL"
class="mw-redirect">NFL</a>
<a
href="/wiki/Super_Bowl_XXXVIII?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Super
Bowl
XXXVIII">Super
Bowl
XXXVIII</a>.</p>








<div
class="thumb
tright">









<div
class="thumbinner"
style="width:302px;">









<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:HaseAufCenterstage.jpg"
target="_blank"
class="image"><img
alt=""
src="http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/HaseAufCenterstage.jpg/300px-HaseAufCenterstage.jpg"
width="300"
height="127"
class="thumbimage"
srcset="http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/HaseAufCenterstage.jpg/450px-HaseAufCenterstage.jpg
1.5x,
http://rpmedia.ask.com/ts?u=/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/HaseAufCenterstage.jpg/600px-HaseAufCenterstage.jpg
2x"
/></a>










<div
class="thumbcaption">











<div
class="magnify">











<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:HaseAufCenterstage.jpg"
target="_blank"
class="internal"
title="Enlarge"><img
src="http://sp.ask.com/sh/i/wiki/magnify-clip.png"
width="15"
height="11"
alt=""
/></a>










</div>
Green
Day
live
in
Germany
during
the











<i>American
Idiot</i>
tour.









</div>









</div>








</div>








<p>The
resulting
album,
<i><a
href="/wiki/American_Idiot?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="American
Idiot">American
Idiot</a></i>
(2004),
debuted
at
number
one
on
the
Billboard
charts,
the
band's
first
album
to
reach
number
one,
backed
by
the
success
of
the
album's
first
single,
<i><a
href="/wiki/American_Idiot_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="American
Idiot
(song)">American
Idiot</a></i>.
The
album
was
labeled
as
a
<i>punk
<a
href="/wiki/Rock_opera?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rock
opera">rock
opera</a></i>
which
follows
the
journey
of
the
fictitious
<i><a
href="/wiki/Jesus_of_Suburbia?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jesus
of
Suburbia">Jesus
of
Suburbia</a></i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-35"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
album
depicts
the
modern
American
life
under
the
control
from
an
idiot
ruler
who
let
people
be
misinformed
by
media
as
well
as
inserted
&quot;redneck
agenda&quot;.
It
gives
different
angles
on
an
everyman,
modern
icons,
and
leaders
on
the
topic.<sup
id="cite_ref-:0_36-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-:0-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup>
Released
two
months
before
U.S.
President
<a
href="/wiki/George_W._Bush?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="George
W.
Bush">George
W.
Bush</a>
was
reelected,
the
album
became
protest
art.<sup
id="cite_ref-37"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup>
<i>American
Idiot</i>
won
the
<a
href="/wiki/47th_Grammy_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="47th
Grammy
Awards"
class="mw-redirect">2005
Grammy</a>
for
<i><a
href="/wiki/Best_Rock_Album?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Best
Rock
Album"
class="mw-redirect">Best
Rock
Album</a></i>.
The
band
also
won
a
total
of
seven
awards
out
of
eight
awards
for
which
they
were
nominated,
including
the
Viewer's
Choice
Award
in
<a
href="/wiki/MTV_Video_Music_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="MTV
Video
Music
Awards"
class="mw-redirect">MTV
Video
Music
Awards</a>
2005.<sup
id="cite_ref-38"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Through
2005,
the
band
toured
in
support
of
the
album
with
nearly
150
dates
(Longest
tour
in
their
career)
visiting
Japan,
Australia,
South
America
and
the
United
Kingdom.
While
touring
for
<i>American
Idiot</i>,
they
filmed
and
recorded
the
two
concerts
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Milton_Keynes?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Milton
Keynes">Milton
Keynes</a>
<a
href="/wiki/National_Bowl?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="National
Bowl">National
Bowl</a>
in
England,
which
was
voted
'The
Best
Show
On
Earth'
in
a
<i><a
href="/wiki/Kerrang!?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Kerrang!">Kerrang!</a></i>
Magazine
Poll.
These
recordings
were
released
as
a
live
CD
and
DVD
called
<i><a
href="/wiki/Bullet_in_a_Bible?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Bullet
in
a
Bible">Bullet
in
a
Bible</a></i>
on
November
15,
2005.
This
CD/DVD
featured
songs
from
<i>American
Idiot</i>
as
well
as
songs
from
all
its
previous
albums,
except
<i>Kerplunk</i>
and
<i>1,039/Smoothed
Out
Slappy
Hours</i>.
The
DVD
featured
behind-the-scenes
footage
of
the
band,
and
showed
how
the
band
prepared
to
put
on
the
show.
The
final
shows
of
its
2005
world
tour
were
in
Sydney
and
<a
href="/wiki/Melbourne?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Melbourne">Melbourne</a>
in
Australia,
on
December
14
and
17
respectively.</p>








<p>On
August
1,
2005
Green
Day
announced
that
it
had
rescinded
the
master
rights
to
its
pre-<i>Dookie</i>
material
from
Lookout!
Records,
citing
a
continuing
<a
href="/wiki/Breach_of_contract?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Breach
of
contract">breach
of
contract</a>
regarding
unpaid
royalties,
a
complaint
shared
with
other
Lookout!
bands.<sup
id="cite_ref-39"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>On
January
10,
2006
the
band
was
awarded
with
a
<a
href="/wiki/People%27s_Choice_Award?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="People's
Choice
Award"
class="mw-redirect">People's
Choice
Award</a>
as
favorite
musical
group
or
band.<sup
id="cite_ref-40"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

class="mw-headline"

<p>Green
Day
engaged
in
a
number
of
other
smaller
projects
in
the
time
following
the
success
of
<i>American
Idiot</i>.
The
group
released
an
album
under
the
name
<a
href="/wiki/Foxboro_Hot_Tubs?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Foxboro
Hot
Tubs">Foxboro
Hot
Tubs</a>
entitled
<i><a
href="/wiki/Stop_Drop_and_Roll!!!?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Stop
Drop
and
Roll!!!">Stop
Drop
and
Roll!!!</a></i>
In
2008,
the
Foxboro
Hot
Tubs
went
on
a
mini-tour
to
promote
the
record,
hitting
tiny
Bay
Area
venues
including
the
Stork
Club
in
Oakland
and
Toot's
Tavern
in
<a
href="/wiki/Crockett,_California?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Crockett,
California">Crockett,
California</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-41"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

class="thumb
tleft">

<p>In
an
interview
with
Carson
Daly,
<a
href="/wiki/Garbage_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Garbage
(band)">Garbage</a>
lead
singer
<a
href="/wiki/Shirley_Manson?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Shirley
Manson">Shirley
Manson</a>
revealed
that
<a
href="/wiki/Butch_Vig?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Butch
Vig">Butch
Vig</a>
would
be
producing
Green
Day's
forthcoming
album.<sup
id="cite_ref-42"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
span
of
nearly
five
years
between
<i>American
Idiot</i>
and
<i>21st
Century
Breakdown</i>
was
the
longest
gap
between
studio
albums
in
Green
Day's
career.
The
band
had
been
working
on
new
material
since
January
2006.
By
October
2007,
Armstrong
had
45
songs
written,
but
the
band
showed
no
further
signs
of
progress
until
October
2008,
when
two
videos
showing
the
band
recording
in
the
studio
with
producer
Butch
Vig
were
posted
on
YouTube.<sup
id="cite_ref-43"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
writing
and
recording
process,
spanning
three
years
and
four
recording
studios,
was
finally
finished
in
April
2009.<sup
id="cite_ref-44"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p><i><a
href="/wiki/21st_Century_Breakdown?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="21st
Century
Breakdown">21st
Century
Breakdown</a></i>,
was
released
on
May
15,
2009.<sup
id="cite_ref-45"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
album
received
a
mainly
positive
reception
from
critics,
getting
an
average
rating
between
3
and
4
stars.<sup
id="cite_ref-46"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-47"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup>
After
the
release,
the
album
reached
number
one
in
fourteen
countries,
being
certified
gold
or
platinum
in
each.
<i>21st
Century
Breakdown</i>
achieved
Green
Day's
best
chart
performance
to
date.
The
band
started
playing
shows
in
California
in
April
and
early
May.
It
was
their
first
live
show
in
about
three
years.
Green
Day
went
on
a
world
tour
that
started
in
North
America
in
July
2009
and
continuing
around
the
world
throughout
the
rest
of
2009
and
early
2010.<sup
id="cite_ref-livedaily_48-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-livedaily-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p><a
href="/wiki/Wal-Mart?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Wal-Mart"
class="mw-redirect">Wal-Mart</a>
refused
to
carry
the
album
as
it
contains
a
<a
href="/wiki/Parental_Advisory?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Parental
Advisory">Parental
Advisory</a>
sticker
and
requested
that
Green
Day
release
a
censored
edition.
The
band
members
did
not
wish
to
change
any
lyrics
on
the
album
and
responded
by
stating,
&quot;There's
nothing
dirty
about
our
record...
They
want
artists
to
censor
their
records
in
order
to
be
carried
in
there.
We
just
said
no.
We've
never
done
it
before.
You
feel
like
you're
in
1953
or
something.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-49"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-50"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
2009,
the
band
met
with
award-winning
director
<a
href="/wiki/Michael_Mayer_(director)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Michael
Mayer
(director)">Michael
Mayer</a>
and
many
cast
and
crew
members
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/Tony_Award?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tony
Award">Tony
Award</a>-winning
musical
<i><a
href="/wiki/Spring_Awakening?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Spring
Awakening">Spring
Awakening</a></i>
to
create
a
stage
version
of
the
album
<i>American
Idiot</i>.<sup
id="cite_ref-americanidiotmusii_51-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-americanidiotmusii-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-americanitiotcharaters_52-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-americanitiotcharaters-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup>
<i><a
href="/wiki/American_Idiot_(musical)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="American
Idiot
(musical)">American
Idiot:
The
Musical</a></i>
opened
in
the
<a
href="/wiki/Berkeley_Repertory_Theatre?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Berkeley
Repertory
Theatre">Berkeley
Repertory
Theatre</a>
during
the
end
of
2009.<sup
id="cite_ref-americanidiotmusii_51-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-americanidiotmusii-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
show
features
an
expanded
story
of
the
original
album,
with
new
characters
such
as
Will,
Extraordinary
Girl,
and
Favorite
Son.<sup
id="cite_ref-americanitiotcharaters_52-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-americanitiotcharaters-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
April
20,
2010,
<i>American
Idiot:
The
Musical</i>
opened
on
Broadway,
and
Green
Day
released
the
<a
href="/wiki/American_Idiot:_The_Original_Broadway_Cast_Recording?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="American
Idiot:
The
Original
Broadway
Cast
Recording">soundtrack</a>
to
the
musical,
featuring
a
new
song
by
Green
Day
entitled
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/When_It%27s_Time?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="When
It's
Time">When
It's
Time</a>&quot;.
In
June
2010
the
<a
href="/wiki/ITunes?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="ITunes">iTunes</a>
received
the
single
&quot;When
It's
Time&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-53"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>During
the
<a
href="/wiki/Spike_Video_Game_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Spike
Video
Game
Awards">Spike
TV
Video
Game
Awards
2009</a>,
it
was
announced
that
Green
Day
was
set
to
have
its
own
<i>Rock
Band</i>
video
game
titled
as
<i><a
href="/wiki/Green_Day:_Rock_Band?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Green
Day:
Rock
Band">Green
Day:
Rock
Band</a></i>,
as
a
follow-up
to
the
last
band
specific
<i>Rock
Band</i>
game,
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Beatles:_Rock_Band?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Beatles:
Rock
Band">The
Beatles:
Rock
Band</a></i>.
The
game
features
the
full
albums
of
<i><a
href="/wiki/Dookie?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Dookie">Dookie</a></i>,
<i><a
href="/wiki/American_Idiot?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="American
Idiot">American
Idiot</a></i>,
and
<i><a
href="/wiki/21st_Century_Breakdown?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="21st
Century
Breakdown">21st
Century
Breakdown</a></i>
as
well
as
select
songs
from
the
rest
of
Green
Day's
discography.<sup
id="cite_ref-hmxpresser_54-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-hmxpresser-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-g4tv_pax_east_55-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-g4tv_pax_east-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>During
the
second
leg
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/21st_Century_Breakdown_World_Tour?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="21st
Century
Breakdown
World
Tour">21st
Century
Breakdown
World
Tour</a>
the
band
had
said
that
they
are
writing
new
material.<sup
id="cite_ref-56"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
an
interview
with
<i><a
href="/wiki/Kerrang!?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Kerrang!">Kerrang!</a></i>
magazine,
Armstrong
spoke
about
the
possible
new
album:
&quot;We
did
some
demos
in
Berlin,
some
in
Stockholm,
some
just
outside
of
Glasgow
and
some
in
Amsterdam.
We
wanted
get
[the
songs]
down
in
some
early
form.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-57"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
band
also
stated
that
they
were
recording
a
live
album
during
the
entire
tour
on
the
last
date
of
the
tour
in
<a
href="/wiki/Mountain_View,_California?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mountain
View,
California">Mountain
View,
California</a>,
also
before
playing
the
song
&quot;Cigarettes
and
Valentines&quot;.
In
October
2010,
Dirnt
was
interviewed
by
Radio
W,
mentioning
that
they
have
completed
the
writing
process
of
the
ninth
studio
album.
In
the
interview,
Dirnt
also
mentioned
that
a
new
live
album
will
&quot;most
likely&quot;
be
released.<sup
id="cite_ref-58"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
live
CD/DVD
and
CD/Blu-ray
entitled
<i><a
href="/wiki/Awesome_as_Fuck?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Awesome
as
Fuck">Awesome
as
Fuck</a></i>
was
released
on
March
22,
2011.<sup
id="cite_ref-Rutherford_59-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Rutherford-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-press_release_60-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-press_release-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

<p>During
the
end
of
2011,
the
band
played
several
secret
shows
(under
the
name
<a
href="/wiki/Foxboro_Hot_Tubs?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Foxboro
Hot
Tubs">Foxboro
Hot
Tubs</a>)
whose
setlists
consisted
almost
entirely
of
previously
unheard
songs.
Green
Day
entered
the
studio
and
began
recording
new
material
in
February
2012,
later
announcing
a
trilogy
of
albums
titled
<i>&iexcl;Uno!</i>,
<i>&iexcl;Dos!</i>,
and
<i>&iexcl;Tr&eacute;!</i>
which
would
be
released
in
the
fall
of
2012.<sup
id="cite_ref-Album_Trio_Press_Release_8-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Album_Trio_Press_Release-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-61"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
trilogy
marked
longtime
touring
guitarist
<a
href="/wiki/Jason_White_(musician)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Jason
White
(musician)">Jason
White's</a>
induction
as
the
fourth
member
of
the
band.<sup
id="cite_ref-Alan_Di_Perna_1-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Alan_Di_Perna-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup>
That
summer
Green
Day
played
several
festivals
and
promotional
shows
including
the
<a
href="/wiki/Rock_en_Seine?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rock
en
Seine">Rock
en
Seine</a>
festival
in
France,
the
Rock
am
See
festival
in
Germany,
and
the
<a
href="/wiki/Reading_Festival?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Reading
Festival"
class="mw-redirect">Reading
Festival</a>
in
the
United
Kingdom.<sup
id="cite_ref-62"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-63"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p><i><a
href="/wiki/%C2%A1Uno!?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="&iexcl;Uno!">&iexcl;Uno!</a></i>,
<i><a
href="/wiki/%C2%A1Dos!?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="&iexcl;Dos!">&iexcl;Dos!</a></i>,
and
<i><a
href="/wiki/%C2%A1Tr%C3%A9!?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="&iexcl;Tr&eacute;!">&iexcl;Tr&eacute;!</a></i>
were
released
on
September
21,
November
9,
and
December
7,
2012
respectively
and
were
met
with
generally
positive
reviews.
On
January
22,
2013
the
band
announced
that
<i><a
href="/wiki/%C2%A1Cuatro!?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="&iexcl;Cuatro!">&iexcl;Cuatro!</a></i>,
a
documentary
about
the
making
of
<i>&iexcl;Uno!,
&iexcl;Dos!</i>
and
<i>&iexcl;Tr&eacute;!</i>,
would
premiere
on
January
26
in
Aspen,
Colorado
as
part
of
the
X
Games
FILM
showcase,
and
would
be
released
on
DVD
April
9,
2013.<sup
id="cite_ref-64"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup>
Another
documentary
was
announced
called
<i>Broadway
Idiot</i>
which
focuses
on
the
creation
on
the
<a
href="/wiki/American_Idiot_(musical)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="American
Idiot
(musical)">American
Idiot
musical</a>
and
Armstrong's
run
as
playing
the
character
of
St.
Jimmy.<sup
id="cite_ref-65"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup>
On
March
10,
2013,
Green
Day
began
their
<a
href="/wiki/99_Revolutions_Tour?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="99
Revolutions
Tour">99
Revolutions
Tour</a>
to
support
the
trilogy.<sup
id="cite_ref-66"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Musical_style_and_influences">Musical
style
and
influences</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Green_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8"
title="Edit
section:
Musical
style
and
influences">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<div
class="thumb
tleft">









<div
class="thumbinner"
style="width:222px;">









<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Green_Day_King_for_a_Day.jpg"
target="_blank"
class="image"><img
alt=""

class="thumbimage"

/></a>










<div
class="thumbcaption">











<div
class="magnify">











<a
href="http://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/File:Green_Day_King_for_a_Day.jpg"

class="internal"
