/></a>










</div>
Green
Day
performing
&quot;King
for
a
Day,&quot;
a











<a
href="/wiki/Ska?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ska">ska</a>-inspired
song
featuring
saxophones
and
trumpets.









</div>









</div>








</div>








<p>Green
Day's
sound
is
often
compared
to
first
wave
punk
bands
such
as
the
<a
href="/wiki/Ramones?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Ramones">Ramones</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/The_Clash?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Clash">The
Clash</a>,
<a
href="/wiki/Sex_Pistols?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sex
Pistols">Sex
Pistols</a>,
The
Jam,
and
the
<a
href="/wiki/Buzzcocks?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Buzzcocks">Buzzcocks</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-snotty_24-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-snotty-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup>
Citing
the
band's
musical
style
prevalent
on
<i>Dookie</i>,
Stephen
Erlewine
of
<a
href="/wiki/Allmusic?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Allmusic"
class="mw-redirect">Allmusic</a>
described
Green
Day
as
&quot;punk
revivalists
who
recharged
the
energy
of
speedy,
catchy
three-chord
punk-pop
songs.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-AllmusicBio_67-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-AllmusicBio-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup>
While
Armstrong
is
the
primary
songwriter,
he
looks
to
the
other
band
members
for
organizational
help.<sup
id="cite_ref-68"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup>
Billie
Joe
Armstrong
has
mentioned
that
some
of
his
biggest
influences
are
seminal
<a
href="/wiki/Alternative_rock?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Alternative
rock">alternative
rock</a>
bands
<a
href="/wiki/H%C3%BCsker_D%C3%BC?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="H&uuml;sker
D&uuml;">H&uuml;sker
D&uuml;</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/The_Replacements_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Replacements
(band)">The
Replacements</a>,
and
that
their
influence
is
particularly
noted
in
the
band's
chord
changes
in
songs.<sup
id="cite_ref-snotty_24-2"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-snotty-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup>
Green
Day
has
covered
H&uuml;sker
D&uuml;'s
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Don%27t_Want_to_Know_If_You_Are_Lonely?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Don't
Want
to
Know
If
You
Are
Lonely">Don't
Want
to
Know
If
You
Are
Lonely</a>&quot;
as
a
b-side
to
the
&quot;Warning&quot;
single,
and
the
character
&quot;Mr.
Whirly&quot;
in
their
song
&quot;Misery&quot;
is
a
reference
to
the
Replacements
song
of
the
same
name.<sup
id="cite_ref-69"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup>
Among
other
influences,
Green
Day
have
also
cited
<a
href="/wiki/The_Who?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Who">The
Who</a>
and
<a
href="/wiki/Power_pop?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Power
pop">power
pop</a>
pioneers
<a
href="/wiki/Cheap_Trick?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Cheap
Trick">Cheap
Trick</a>.<sup
id="cite_ref-Spin_Interview_70-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-Spin_Interview-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup>
English
rock
musician
<a
href="/wiki/Noel_Gallagher?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Noel
Gallagher">Noel
Gallagher</a>
of
<a
href="/wiki/Oasis_(band)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Oasis
(band)">Oasis</a>
complained
about
the
band
semi-jokingly,
claiming
that
they
ripped
off
his
song
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Wonderwall_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Wonderwall
(song)">Wonderwall</a>&quot;
with
their
song
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Boulevard_of_Broken_Dreams_(Green_Day_song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Boulevard
of
Broken
Dreams
(Green
Day
song)">Boulevard
of
Broken
Dreams</a>&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-71"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Related_projects">Related
projects</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Green_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9"
title="Edit
section:
Related
projects">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<div
class="rellink
relarticle
mainarticle">








Main
article:









<a
href="/wiki/Green_Day_related_projects?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Green
Day
related
projects">Green
Day
related
projects</a>







</div>








<p>Since
1991,
members
of
the
band
have
branched
out
past
Green
Day
and
have
started
other
projects
with
other
musicians.
Notable
related
projects
of
Green
Day
include
Billie
Joe
Armstrong's
<a
href="/wiki/Pinhead_Gunpowder?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Pinhead
Gunpowder">Pinhead
Gunpowder</a>
(which
also
features
Green
Day's
guitarist
Jason
White),
<a
href="/wiki/The_Frustrators?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Frustrators">The
Frustrators</a>
in
which
Mike
Dirnt
plays
bass,
and
<a
href="/wiki/The_Network?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Network">The
Network</a>,
a
collaboration
between
Green
Day
and
members
of
the
band,
<a
href="/wiki/Devo?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Devo">Devo</a>
in
which
all
members
play
under
fake
stage
names.<sup
id="cite_ref-72"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup>
Green
Day
has
also
released
an
album
titled
<i><a
href="/wiki/Stop_Drop_and_Roll!!!?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Stop
Drop
and
Roll!!!">Stop
Drop
and
Roll!!!</a></i>
on
May
20,
2008,
under
the
name
<a
href="/wiki/Foxboro_Hot_Tubs?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Foxboro
Hot
Tubs">Foxboro
Hot
Tubs</a>,
they
currently
use
this
name
to
book
secret
shows.<sup
id="cite_ref-73"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
late
December
2011,
Armstrong
formed
a
new
side
band
called
The
Boo
along
his
wife
<a
href="/wiki/Adrienne_Armstrong?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Adrienne
Armstrong">Adrienne</a>
and
their
two
sons.</p>








<p>In
September
2006,
Green
Day
collaborated
with
<a
href="/wiki/U2?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="U2">U2</a>
and
producer
<a
href="/wiki/Rick_Rubin?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rick
Rubin">Rick
Rubin</a>
to
record
a
cover
of
the
song
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/The_Saints_Are_Coming?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Saints
Are
Coming">The
Saints
Are
Coming</a>&quot;,
originally
recorded
by
<a
href="/wiki/The_Skids?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Skids"
class="mw-redirect">The
Skids</a>,
with
an
accompanying
video.
The
song
was
recorded
to
benefit
<a
href="/wiki/Music_Rising?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Music
Rising">Music
Rising</a>,
an
organization
to
help
raise
money
for
musicians'
instruments
lost
during
<a
href="/wiki/Hurricane_Katrina?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hurricane
Katrina">Hurricane
Katrina</a>,
and
to
bring
awareness
on
the
eve
of
the
one-year
anniversary
of
the
disaster.<sup
id="cite_ref-74"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>In
December
2006,
Green
Day
and
<a
href="/wiki/Natural_Resources_Defense_Council?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Natural
Resources
Defense
Council">NRDC</a>
opened
a
web
site
in
partnership
to
raise
awareness
on
America's
dependency
on
oil.<sup
id="cite_ref-75"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup><sup
id="cite_ref-76"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Green
Day
released
a
cover
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/John_Lennon?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="John
Lennon">John
Lennon</a>
song
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Working_Class_Hero?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Working
Class
Hero">Working
Class
Hero</a>&quot;,
which
was
featured
on
the
album
<i><a
href="/wiki/Instant_Karma:_The_Amnesty_International_Campaign_to_Save_Darfur?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Instant
Karma:
The
Amnesty
International
Campaign
to
Save
Darfur">Instant
Karma:
The
Amnesty
International
Campaign
to
Save
Darfur</a></i>.
The
band
performed
the
song
on
the
season
finale
of
<i><a
href="/wiki/American_Idol?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="American
Idol">American
Idol</a></i>.
The
song
was
nominated
for
a
<a
href="/wiki/50th_Grammy_Awards?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="50th
Grammy
Awards"
class="mw-redirect">Grammy
Award
in
2008</a>
but
lost
to
<a
href="/wiki/The_White_Stripes?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
White
Stripes">The
White
Stripes</a>'
&quot;<a
href="/wiki/Icky_Thump?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Icky
Thump">Icky
Thump</a>&quot;.
That
summer,
the
band
appeared
in
a
cameo
role
in
<i><a
href="/wiki/The_Simpsons_Movie?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Simpsons
Movie">The
Simpsons
Movie</a></i>,
where
they
perform
<a
href="/wiki/The_Simpsons_Theme?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
Simpsons
Theme">the
show's
theme
song</a>.
Their
version
was
released
as
a
single
on
July
24,
2007.</p>








<p>In
2009,
the
band
collaborated
with
theatre
director
<a
href="/wiki/Michael_Mayer_(director)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Michael
Mayer
(director)">Michael
Mayer</a>
to
adapt
their
<a
href="/wiki/Rock_opera?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rock
opera">rock
opera</a>
<i>American
Idiot</i>
into
a
one-act
stage
<a
href="/wiki/American_Idiot_(musical)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="American
Idiot
(musical)">musical</a>
that
premiered
at
the
<a
href="/wiki/Berkeley_Rep?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Berkeley
Rep"
class="mw-redirect">Berkeley
Rep</a>
on
September
15,
2009.
The
show
then
moved
to
Broadway
on
April
20,
2010.</p>








<p>The
reviews
of
<i>American
Idiot:
The
Musical</i>
have
been
positive
to
mixed.
Charles
Isherwood
of
<a
href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
New
York
Times">The
New
York
Times</a>
wrote
an
enthusiastic
review
for
the
Broadway
production.
He
called
the
show
&quot;a
pulsating
portrait
of
wasted
youth
that
invokes
all
the
standard
genre
conventions
...
only
to
transcend
them
through
the
power
of
its
music
and
the
artistry
of
its
execution,
the
show
is
as
invigorating
and
ultimately
as
moving
as
anything
Iâ€™ve
seen
on
Broadway
this
season.
Or
maybe
for
a
few
seasons
past.&quot;
Jed
Gottlieb
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/Boston_Herald?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Boston
Herald">Boston
Herald</a>
enjoyed
the
premise
of
the
show
but
found
that
&quot;the
music
and
message
suffer
in
a
setting
where
the
audience
is
politely,
soberly
seated&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-77"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>Michael
Kuchiwara
of
the
<a
href="/wiki/Associated_Press?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Associated
Press">Associated
Press</a>
found
the
show
to
be
&quot;visually
striking
[and]
musically
adventurous&quot;,
but
noted
that
&quot;the
show
has
the
barest
wisp
of
a
story
and
minimal
character
development&quot;.
Paul
Kolnik
in
<a
href="/wiki/USA_Today?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="USA
Today">USA
Today</a>
enjoyed
the
contradiction
that
Green
Day's
&quot;massively
popular,
starkly
disenchanted
album
...
would
be
the
feel-good
musical
of
the
season&quot;.
<i>Time</i>
magazine's
Richard
Zoglin
opined
that
the
score
&quot;is
as
pure
a
specimen
of
contemporary
punk
rock
as
Broadway
has
yet
encountered
[yet]
there's
enough
variety.
...
Where
the
show
fall
short
is
as
a
fully
developed
narrative.&quot;
He
concluded
that
&quot;<i>American
Idiot</i>,
despite
its
earnest
huffing
and
puffing,
remains
little
more
than
an
annotated
rock
concert.
...
Still,
[it]
deserves
at
least
two
cheers
â€“
for
its
irresistible
musical
energy
and
for
opening
fresh
vistas
for
that
odd
couple,
rock
and
Broadway.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-78"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup>
Peter
Travers
from
<a
href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rolling
Stone">Rolling
Stone</a>,
in
his
review
of
<i>American
Idiot</i>,
wrote
&quot;Though
<i>American
Idiot</i>
carries
echoes
of
such
rock
musicals
as
<i><a
href="/wiki/Tommy_(album)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Tommy
(album)">Tommy</a></i>,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Hair_(musical)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Hair
(musical)">Hair</a></i>,
<i><a
href="/wiki/Rent_(musical)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rent
(musical)">Rent</a></i>
and
<i><a
href="/wiki/Spring_Awakening?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Spring
Awakening">Spring
Awakening</a></i>,
it
cuts
its
own
path
to
the
heart.
You
wonâ€™t
know
what
hit
you.
<i>American
Idiot</i>
knows
no
limitsâ€”it's
a
global
knockout.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-79"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup>
The
musical
has
been
nominated
for
three
<a

<p>In
October
2009,
a
Green
Day
art
project
was
exhibited
at
StolenSpace
Gallery
in
London.
The
exhibition
showed
artworks
created
for
each
of
the
songs
on
<i>21st
Century
Breakdown</i>,
was
supported
by
the
band,
and
led
by
their
manager
Pat
Magnarella.<sup
id="cite_ref-80"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup>
He
explained
in
an
interview
that
&quot;[Artists
are]
basically
like
rock
bands.
Most
are
creating
their
art,
but
don't
know
how
to
promote
it.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-81"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup>
For
Billie
Joe
Armstrong,
&quot;Many
of
the
artists...
show
their
work
on
the
street,
and
we
feel
a
strong
connection
to
that
type
of
creative
expression.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-82"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>On

of
<i><a

Michael

(Green

<i><a

<h2><span
class="mw-headline"
id="Controversy">Controversy</span>
<span
class="mw-editsection">[<a
href="/wiki?title=Green_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10"
title="Edit
section:
Controversy">edit</a>]</span></h2>








<p>The
band
has
generated
controversy
over
whether
the
band's
musical
style
and
major-label
status
constitutes
as
&quot;true
<a
href="/wiki/Punk_rock?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Punk
rock">punk</a>&quot;.<sup
id="cite_ref-softpedia2005_87-0"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-softpedia2005-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup>
In
reaction
to
both
the
style
of
music
and
the
background
of
the
band,
<a
href="/wiki/John_Lydon?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="John
Lydon">John
Lydon</a>,
former
front
man
of
the
1970s
punk
band
the
<a
href="/wiki/Sex_Pistols?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Sex
Pistols">Sex
Pistols</a>
commented:</p>








<blockquote>









<p>&quot;So
there
we
are
fending
off
all
that
and
it
pisses
me
off
that
years
later
a
wank
outfit
like
Green
Day
hop
in
and
nick
all
that
and
attach
it
to
themselves.
They
didn't
earn
their
wings
to
do
that
and
if
they
were
true
punk
they
wouldn't
look
anything
like
they
do.&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-88"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








</blockquote>








<p>Armstrong
himself
has
discussed
the
group's
status
of
being
a
punk
band
on
a
major
record
label,
saying
&quot;Sometimes
I
think
we've
become
totally
redundant
because
we're
this
big
band
now,
we've
made
a
lot
of
money
â€“
we're
not
punk
rock
any
more.
But
then
I
think
about
it
and
just
say,
'You
can
take
us
out
of
a
punk
rock
environment,
but
you
can't
take
the
punk
rock
out
of
us.'&quot;<sup
id="cite_ref-softpedia2005_87-1"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-softpedia2005-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup></p>








<p>On
September
21,
2012,
while
Green
Day
was
performing
at
the
iHeartRadio
music
festival,
lead
vocalist/guitarist
<a
href="/wiki/Billie_Joe_Armstrong?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Billie
Joe
Armstrong">Billie
Joe
Armstrong</a>
stopped
while
performing
<a
href="/wiki/Basket_Case_(song)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Basket
Case
(song)">Basket
Case</a>,
because
he
believed
their
time
was
being
shortened,
possibly
in
order
to
extend
R&amp;B
artist
<a
href="/wiki/Usher_(entertainer)?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Usher
(entertainer)">Usher</a>'s
performance.
Angered,
Armstrong
began
ranting
while
a
screen
in
the
rear
of
the
audience
was
labeled
&quot;1
Minutes
Left&quot;,
saying
&quot;You're
not
gonna
give
me
one
fucking
minute?
You've
gotta
be
fucking
kidding
me!&quot;.
He
also
told
the
crowd
he
was
not
<a
href="/wiki/Justin_Bieber?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Justin
Bieber">Justin
Bieber</a>
and
labeled
the
festival
as
a
&quot;joke&quot;.
When
the
screen
went
blank,
Armstrong
smashed
his
guitar,
while
bassist
<a
href="/wiki/Mike_Dirnt?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Mike
Dirnt">Mike
Dirnt</a>
smashed
his
bass.
Armstrong
then
gave
<a
href="/wiki/The_finger?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="The
finger">the
finger</a>,
and
declared
that
Green
Day
would
be
back
before
throwing
his
microphone
down
and
walking
off
the
stage.<sup
id="cite_ref-89"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup>
Two
days
later,
the
band's
representative
apologized
for
the
incident
on
their
behalf
stating
that
&quot;Green
Day
would
like
everyone
to
know
that
their
set
was
not
cut
short
by
Clear
Channel
and
to
apologize
to
those
they
offended
at
the
iHeartRadio
Festival
in
Las
Vegas&quot;
also
adding
that
Armstrong
will
be
headed
to
<a
href="/wiki/Drug_rehabilitation?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Drug
rehabilitation">rehab</a>,
for
abuse
of
alcohol
and
prescription
pills
for
anxiety
and
insomnia.<sup
id="cite_ref-90"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup>
However
Mike
Dirnt
would
later
say
in
an
interview
with
<i><a
href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone?qsrc=3044"
onmousedown="triggerActionLog('primaryContent','','center','click','primaryContent','','');"
title="Rolling
Stone">Rolling
Stone</a></i>
that
he
agreed
with
what
Billie
Joe
meant
by
his
rant.<sup
id="cite_ref-91"
class="reference"><a
href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup></p>

afc_match()
{

=

{












count
=
window['ad_config_top'];








}









var
countBottom
=
0;








if(window['ad_config_bot'])
{












countBottom
=
window['ad_config_bot'];








}









if(window['backfillParam'])
{




























window['backfillParam']['pl_bmodn']
=
5;
























window['backfillParam']['pl_tnum']
=
count;












window['backfillParam']['pl_bnum']
=
countBottom;








}


































var
_matchUrl
=
"/afc-match?q=Green_Day&page=1&ac=24&qid=93E831669C747EC5B6E24CDEB710795E&qsrc=121&dm=&qrt=2&lid="+
"&o=0&l=dir&oo=&cl=ca-aj-cat&ch=cx_ask_wiki,ad_dirN";





















_matchUrl+=
"&userip=76.78.3.114";




































_matchUrl+="&losid=a&locid=encw&lodid=us&loaid=a16";









var
location
=
window.location
+
"";








location
=
location.substring(7);








var
cutIdx
=
location.indexOf("/");








if
(location.indexOf(":")
>
-1)
{




















cutIdx
=
1
+
cutIdx
+
location.substring(cutIdx+1).indexOf("/");








}









var
urlPrefix
=
location.substring(0,
cutIdx);








_matchUrl
=
"http://"
+
urlPrefix
+
_matchUrl
+
"&afcec="
+
count
+
"&afcecb="
+
countBottom;








ajax_get(_matchUrl,
null,
null);




}





function
getXHR()
{








if
(window.XMLHttpRequest)
{












return
new
XMLHttpRequest();








}
else
if
(window.ActiveXObject)
{












try
{
















return
new
ActiveXObject("Msxml2.XMLHTTP");












}
catch
(e)
{
















try
{




















return
new
ActiveXObject("Microsoft.XMLHTTP");
















}
catch
(E)
{




















return
null;
















}












}








}








else
{












return
null;








}




}





function
ajax_get(url,
onsuccess,
onerror)
{








var
obj
=
getXHR();








if(obj)
{












obj.onreadystatechange
=
function()
{
















if(obj.readyState==4)
{




















if
(obj.status
==
200
&&
typeof(onsuccess)
==
"function")
{
























onsuccess(obj);




















}
else
if
(typeof(onerror)
==
"function")
{
























onerror(obj);




















}






















try
{
























delete
obj['onreadystatechange'];




















}
catch(e)
{}
















}












};












obj.open("GET",
url,
true,
"",
"");












obj.send(null);












return
obj;








}
else
{












if(onerror)
{
















onerror("Error
creating
XHR");












}
else
{
















a10.debug("Error
creating
XHR");












}












return
null;








}




}





afc_match();
